			<div id="bodyContent" class="content"><div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><script>function mfTempOpenSection(id){var block=document.getElementById("mf-section-"+id);block.className+=" open-block";block.previousSibling.className+=" open-block";}</script><div class="mw-parser-output"><section class="mf-section-0" id="mf-section-0">
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">For the former railway station in Melbourne, see <a href="/wiki/General_Motors_railway_station" title="General Motors railway station">General Motors railway station</a>.</div>
<p class="mw-empty-elt">
</p>
<p><b>General Motors Company</b>,<sup id="cite_ref-filing_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-filing-1">[1]</a></sup> commonly referred to as <b>General Motors</b> (<b>GM</b>), is an American <a href="/wiki/Multinational_corporation" title="Multinational corporation">multinational corporation</a> headquartered in <a href="/wiki/Detroit" title="Detroit">Detroit</a> that designs, manufactures, markets, and distributes vehicles and vehicle parts, and sells financial services, with global headquarters in Detroit's <a href="/wiki/Renaissance_Center" title="Renaissance Center">Renaissance Center</a>. It was originally founded by <a href="/wiki/William_C._Durant" title="William C. Durant">William C. Durant</a> on September 16, 1908 as a holding company. The company is the largest American automobile manufacturer, and one of the world's largest.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[7]</a></sup> As of 2019, General Motors is ranked #13 on the <a href="/wiki/Fortune_500" title="Fortune 500">Fortune 500</a> rankings of the largest United States corporations by total revenue.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[8]</a></sup></p><table class="infobox vcard" style="width:22em"><caption class="fn org">General Motors Company</caption><tbody><tr><td colspan="2" class="logo" It also either owns or holds a significant stake in foreign brands such as <a href="/wiki/Holden" title="Holden">Holden</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wuling_Motors" title="Wuling Motors">Wuling</a>, <a href="/wiki/Baojun" title="Baojun">Baojun</a>, and <a href="/wiki/FAW_Jiefang" title="FAW Jiefang">Jiefang</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-gmbrands_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gmbrands-11">[10]</a></sup> Annual worldwide sales volume reached a milestone of 10 million vehicles in 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-CNN-2017-02-07_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CNN-2017-02-07-12">[11]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[12]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[13]</a></sup></p>

</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(1)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Business_units">Business units</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=General_Motors&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Business units" data-section="1" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-1 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-1">
<p>In addition to its twelve brands, General Motors holds a 20% stake in <a href="/wiki/Industries_M%C3%A9caniques_Maghr%C3%A9bines" title="Industries Mécaniques Maghrébines">IMM</a>, and a 77% stake in <a href="/wiki/GM_Korea" title="GM Korea">GM Korea</a>. It also has a number of joint-ventures, including <a href="/wiki/Shanghai_GM" class="mw-redirect" title="Shanghai GM">Shanghai GM</a>, <a href="/wiki/SAIC-GM-Wuling_Automobile" class="mw-redirect" title="SAIC-GM-Wuling Automobile">SAIC-GM-Wuling</a> and <a href="/wiki/FAW-GM" title="FAW-GM">FAW-GM</a> in China, <a href="/wiki/GM_Uzbekistan" title="GM Uzbekistan">GM Uzbekistan</a>, <a href="/wiki/General_Motors_India_Private_Limited" class="mw-redirect" title="General Motors India Private Limited">General Motors India</a>, <a href="/wiki/General_Motors_Egypt" title="General Motors Egypt">General Motors Egypt</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Isuzu_Truck_South_Africa" class="mw-redirect" title="Isuzu Truck South Africa">Isuzu Truck South Africa</a>. General Motors employs 212,000 people and does business in more than 140 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-GMemploy_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GMemploy-2">[2]</a></sup> General Motors is divided into four business segments: <i>GM North America</i> (GMNA), <i>GM International Operations</i> (GMIO), <a href="/wiki/Cruise_(autonomous_vehicle)" title="Cruise (autonomous vehicle)">Cruise</a>,  and <i><a href="/wiki/GM_Financial" title="GM Financial">GM Financial</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-GMannualreport2011_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GMannualreport2011-15">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>12, 13</span></sup></p><p>The company also operates a mobility division called <a href="/wiki/Maven_(car_sharing)" title="Maven (car sharing)">Maven</a>, which operates car-sharing services in the United States, and is studying alternatives to individual vehicle ownership.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[15]</a></sup></p><p><a href="/wiki/GM_Defense" title="GM Defense">GM Defense</a> is General Motors' military defense division, catering to the needs of the military for advanced technology and propulsion systems for military vehicles.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[16]</a></sup></p><p>General Motors led global annual vehicle sales for 77 consecutive years from 1931 through 2007, longer than any other automaker, and is still among the world's largest automakers by vehicle unit sales.<sup id="cite_ref-GALLIGAN_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GALLIGAN-18">[17]</a></sup></p><p>General Motors acts in most countries outside the U.S. via wholly owned subsidiaries, but operates in <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="People's Republic of China">China</a> through ten joint ventures.<sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>18, 96</span></sup><sup id="cite_ref-GMannualreport2011_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GMannualreport2011-15">[14]</a></sup> GM's <a href="/wiki/OnStar" title="OnStar">OnStar</a> subsidiary provides vehicle safety, security and information services.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[18]</a></sup></p><p>In 2009, General Motors shed several brands, closing <a href="/wiki/Saturn_Corporation" title="Saturn Corporation">Saturn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pontiac" title="Pontiac">Pontiac</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hummer" title="Hummer">Hummer</a>, and emerged from a government-backed <a href="/wiki/General_Motors_Chapter_11_reorganization" title="General Motors Chapter 11 reorganization">Chapter 11 reorganization</a>. In 2010, the reorganized GM made an <a href="/wiki/Initial_public_offering" title="Initial public offering">initial public offering</a> that was one of the world's top five largest IPOs to date, and returned to profitability later that year.<sup id="cite_ref-Businessweek_2012-02-16_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Businessweek_2012-02-16-20">[19]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(2)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=General_Motors&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History" data-section="2" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-2 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-2">
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_General_Motors" title="History of General Motors">History of General Motors</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/William_C._Durant" title="William C. Durant">William C. Durant</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Durant-Dort_Carriage_Company" title="Durant-Dort Carriage Company">Durant-Dort Carriage Company</a>, of <a href="/wiki/Flint,_Michigan" title="Flint, Michigan">Flint, Michigan</a>, had become the leading manufacturer of horse-drawn vehicles in the United States by 1900. Durant was averse to automobiles, but fellow Flint businessman James H. Whiting, owner of Flint Wagon Works, sold him the <a href="/wiki/Buick" title="Buick">Buick Motor Company</a> in 1904.<sup id="cite_ref-horses_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-horses-21">[20]</a></sup> Durant formed the <i>General Motors Company</i> in 1908 as a <a href="/wiki/Holding_company" title="Holding company">holding company</a>, with partner <a href="/wiki/Charles_Stewart_Mott" title="Charles Stewart Mott">Charles Stewart Mott</a>. GM's first acquisition was Buick, which Durant already owned, then <a href="/wiki/Oldsmobile" title="Oldsmobile">Oldsmobile</a>, on November 12, 1908. In 1909 Durant brought in <a href="/wiki/Cadillac" title="Cadillac">Cadillac</a>, <a href="/wiki/Elmore_(automobile)" class="mw-redirect" title="Elmore (automobile)">Elmore</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oakland_(automobile)" class="mw-redirect" title="Oakland (automobile)">Oakland</a> (predecessor of <a href="/wiki/Pontiac" title="Pontiac">Pontiac</a>), and the Reliance Motor Truck Company of <a href="/wiki/Owosso,_Michigan" title="Owosso, Michigan">Owosso, Michigan</a> and the Rapid Motor Vehicle Company of <a href="/wiki/Pontiac,_Michigan" title="Pontiac, Michigan">Pontiac, Michigan</a> (predecessors of <a href="/wiki/GMC_(automobile)" title="GMC (automobile)">GMC</a>). Durant over-leveraged the fledgling company in making these acquisitions, and was removed by the board of directors in 1910 at the behest of the bankers who backed the loans to keep GM in business.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[21]</a></sup></p><p>Durant re-entered the automotive industry the following year by co-founding the <a href="/wiki/Chevrolet" title="Chevrolet">Chevrolet Motor Company</a> with Swiss race car driver <a href="/wiki/Louis_Chevrolet" title="Louis Chevrolet">Louis Chevrolet</a> (who left the company bearing his name in 1915). In 1916 GM was reincorporated in <a href="/wiki/Detroit" title="Detroit">Detroit</a> as <i>General Motors Corporation</i>. By 1917 the Chevrolet Motor Company had become successful enough that Durant, with the backing of McLaughlin and <a href="/wiki/Pierre_S._du_Pont" title="Pierre S. du Pont">Pierre S. du Pont</a>, reacquired a controlling interest in GM. Chevrolet Motor Company was consolidated into GM on May 2, 1918. Only two years later du Pont orchestrated the removal of Durant once again and replaced him with <a href="/wiki/Alfred_P._Sloan" title="Alfred P. Sloan">Alfred P. Sloan</a>.
</p><p>Sloan established annual styling changes making previous year's models to be "dated". He also implemented the pricing strategy that all car companies use today. The pricing strategy had Chevrolet, Pontiac, Oldsmobile, Buick and Cadillac priced from least expensive to most, respectively.
</p><p>General Motors grew in prominence surpassing Ford Motors selling just over 50% of car sales in 1962. With the prominence of the company, president of General Motors, Charlie Wilson said it best - “What’s good for General Motors is good for America”.
</p><p>Their industrial dominance was displayed as they manufactured products other than cars and trucks such as Aircraft(North American Aviation), Construction equipment(Terex), Trains(Electro-Motive), appliances(Frigidaire).
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:2007_Chevrolet_Suburban_LT_--_07-10-2010_1.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/2007_Chevrolet_Suburban_LT_--_07-10-2010_1.jpg/220px-2007_Chevrolet_Suburban_LT_--_07-10-2010_1.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="144" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="1845" data-file-height="1208"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 144px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/2007_Chevrolet_Suburban_LT_--_07-10-2010_1.jpg/220px-2007_Chevrolet_Suburban_LT_--_07-10-2010_1.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="144" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:2007_Chevrolet_Suburban_LT_--_07-10-2010_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Chevrolet_Suburban" title="Chevrolet Suburban">Chevrolet Suburban</a>, the longest continuous production automobile nameplate<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[22]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Chapter_11_bankruptcy">Chapter 11 bankruptcy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=General_Motors&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Chapter 11 bankruptcy" data-section="3" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/General_Motors_Chapter_11_reorganization" title="General Motors Chapter 11 reorganization">General Motors Chapter 11 reorganization</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:14_Buick_LaCrosse_(14344035480).jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/14_Buick_LaCrosse_%2814344035480%29.jpg/220px-14_Buick_LaCrosse_%2814344035480%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="136" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="3909" data-file-height="2424"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 136px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/14_Buick_LaCrosse_%2814344035480%29.jpg/220px-14_Buick_LaCrosse_%2814344035480%29.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="136" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:14_Buick_LaCrosse_(14344035480).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Buick_LaCrosse#Second_generation_(2010%E2%80%932016)" title="Buick LaCrosse">2nd generation Buick LaCrosse</a>, an example of GM's revival following its restructuring in the aftermath of the <a href="/wiki/Great_Recession" title="Great Recession">Great Recession</a><sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[23]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[24]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>On July 10, 2009, following <a href="/wiki/Chapter_11,_Title_11,_United_States_Code" title="Chapter 11, Title 11, United States Code">Chapter 11</a> reorganization after an initial filing on June 8 2009,<sup id="cite_ref-NYT-Merced-2009-07-10_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT-Merced-2009-07-10-26">[25]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NYT-Maynard-2009-07-10_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT-Maynard-2009-07-10-27">[26]</a></sup> the original General Motors sold assets and some subsidiaries to an entirely new company including the trademark General Motors. Liabilities were left with the original GM freeing the companies of many liabilites resulting in a new GM.
</p><p>GM emerged from government backed <a href="/wiki/Chapter_11,_Title_11,_United_States_Code" title="Chapter 11, Title 11, United States Code">Chapter 11</a> reorganization after an initial filing on June 8, 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT-Merced-2009-07-10_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT-Merced-2009-07-10-26">[25]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NYT-Maynard-2009-07-10_27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT-Maynard-2009-07-10-27">[26]</a></sup> Through the <a href="/wiki/Troubled_Asset_Relief_Program" title="Troubled Asset Relief Program">Troubled Asset Relief Program</a> the US Treasury invested $49.5 billion in General Motors and recovered $39 billion when it sold its shares on December 9, 2013 resulting in a loss of $10.3 billion. The Treasury invested an additional $17.2 billion into GM's former financing company, GMAC (now Ally). The shares in Ally were sold on December 18, 2014 for $19.6 billion netting $2.4 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-Auto_Industry_Bailout_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Auto_Industry_Bailout-28">[27]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-exit_Ally_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-exit_Ally-29">[28]</a></sup> A study by the Center for Automotive Research found that the GM bailout saved 1.2 million jobs and preserved $34.9 billion in tax revenue.<sup id="cite_ref-Last_Sale_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Last_Sale-30">[29]</a></sup></p><p>Also in 2009 <a href="/wiki/General_Motors_Canada" title="General Motors Canada">General Motors of Canada Limited</a> was not part of the General Motors Chapter 11 Bankruptcy, the company shed several brands, closing <a href="/wiki/Saturn_Corporation" title="Saturn Corporation">Saturn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pontiac" title="Pontiac">Pontiac</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hummer" title="Hummer">Hummer</a>, while selling <a href="/wiki/Saab_Automobile" title="Saab Automobile">Saab Automobile</a> to Dutch automaker <a href="/wiki/Spyker_Cars" title="Spyker Cars">Spyker</a>, and emerged from a government-backed <a href="/wiki/General_Motors_Chapter_11_reorganization" title="General Motors Chapter 11 reorganization">Chapter 11 reorganization</a>. In 2010, the reorganized GM made an <a href="/wiki/Initial_public_offering" title="Initial public offering">initial public offering</a> that was one of the world's top five largest IPOs to date, and returned to profitability later that year.<sup id="cite_ref-Businessweek_2012-02-16_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Businessweek_2012-02-16-20">[19]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[30]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[31]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(3)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Corporate_governance">Corporate governance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=General_Motors&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Corporate governance" data-section="4" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-3 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-3">
<p>Based on global sales, General Motors is routinely among the world's largest automakers.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[32]</a></sup> Headquartered at the <a href="/wiki/Renaissance_Center" title="Renaissance Center">Renaissance Center</a> in Detroit, GM employs approximately 180,000 people around the world. In 2009, General Motors sold 6.5 million cars and trucks globally; in 2010, it sold 8.39 million.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[33]</a></sup></p><p>As of April 2019<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=General_Motors&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, <a href="/wiki/Mary_Barra" title="Mary Barra">Mary Barra</a> is the chief executive officer (CEO) and chairman of the board and Mark Reuss is the president.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[34]</a></sup> The head of design, <a href="/wiki/Edward_T._Welburn" title="Edward T. Welburn">Edward T. Welburn</a>, was the first African American to lead a global automotive design organization, and was the highest ranking African American in the US motor industry in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[35]</a></sup> On April 7, 2016, he announced his retirement from General Motors after 44 years, effective July 1, 2016. He was replaced by <a href="/wiki/Michael_Simcoe" title="Michael Simcoe">Michael Simcoe</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[36]</a></sup></p><p>As part of the company's advertising, Ed Whitacre announced the company's 60-day money-back guarantee and repayment of a $6.7 billion loan from the government ahead of schedule.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[37]</a></sup> On December 12, 2013, GM announced that Mary Barra, 51, executive vice president, Global Product Development, Purchasing and Supply Chain, was elected by the board of directors to become the next CEO of the company succeeding Dan Akerson on January 15, 2014. Barra also joined the GM board.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[38]</a></sup> From June 2009 to March 2011, the company had three chief executive officers and three chief financial officers.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[39]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[40]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Financial_results">Financial results</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=General_Motors&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Financial results" data-section="5" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>The company has reported annual profits since 2010. It can carry forward previous losses to reduce tax liability on future earnings. It earned $4.7 billion in 2010. The <i>Wall Street Journal</i> estimated the tax break, including credits for costs related to pensions and other expenses, can be worth as much as $45 billion over the next 20 years.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[41]</a></sup></p><p>In 2010, General Motors ranked second on the list with 8.5 million units produced globally.<sup id="cite_ref-OICA2010_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OICA2010-43">[42]</a></sup> In 2011, GM returned to the first place with 9.025 million units sold worldwide, corresponding to 11.9% <a href="/wiki/Market_share" title="Market share">market share</a> of the global motor vehicle industry. The top two markets in 2011 were China, with 2,547,203 units, and the United States, with 2,503,820 vehicles sold. The Chevrolet brand was the main contributor to GM performance, with 4.76 million vehicles sold around the world in 2011, a global sales record.<sup id="cite_ref-Sales2011_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sales2011-44">[43]</a></sup></p><p>In May 2013 during a commencement speech, CEO Dan Akerson suggested that GM was on the cusp of rejoining the <a href="/wiki/S%26P_500" class="mw-redirect" title="S&amp;P 500">S&amp;P 500</a> index. GM was removed from the index as it approached bankruptcy in 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[44]</a></sup></p><p>On April 24, 2014, <a href="/wiki/CNNMoney" class="mw-redirect" title="CNNMoney">CNNMoney</a> reported that GM profits fell to $108 million for the first three months of 2014. GM now estimates the cost of their <a href="/wiki/2014_General_Motors_recall" class="mw-redirect" title="2014 General Motors recall">2014 recall</a> due to faulty ignition switches, which have been linked to at least 124 deaths, at $1.5 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[45]</a></sup> Shares of GM were down 16% for the year before the new announcement of GM's lower profits.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[46]</a></sup></p><p>On January 4, 2016, <i><a href="/wiki/Fortune_(magazine)" title="Fortune (magazine)">Fortune</a></i> reported that GM led a $1 billion equity financing in the transportation network company (TNC) <a href="/wiki/Lyft" title="Lyft">Lyft</a>.com.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[47]</a></sup> This was GM's first investment in the ride-sharing ventures and its reported participation ($500,000,000) in the round is considered to be indicative of its efforts towards the future of transportation, which it believes will be "connected, seamless and autonomous".<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[48]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Board_of_Directors">Board of Directors</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=General_Motors&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Board of Directors" data-section="6" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>As of February 2017:<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[49]</a></sup></p>

</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(4)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="World_presence">World presence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=General_Motors&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: World presence" data-section="7" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-4 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-4">

</td></tr></tbody></table><h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="North_America">North America</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=General_Motors&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: North America" data-section="8" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>General Motors Canada Limited is the Canadian allied subsidiary of General Motors. The employees are not all Canadian, as some salaried personnel are from the U.S. and work for the company. GM products focus primarily on its four core divisions — Chevrolet, Cadillac, Buick, and GMC. The GM restructuring has resulted in a lower break-even point for annual sales and renewed profits because of the loss of millions of jobs.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[63]</a></sup></p><p>In mid-2005, GM announced that its corporate chrome power emblem "<a href="/wiki/Mark_of_Excellence" title="Mark of Excellence">Mark of Excellence</a>" would begin appearing on all recently introduced and all-new 2006 model vehicles produced and sold in North America. However, in 2009 the "New GM" reversed this, saying that emphasis on its four core divisions would downplay the GM logo.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[64]</a></sup></p><p>In May 2012, GM recorded an 18.4% market share in the U.S. with stock imported.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[65]</a></sup> In November 2018, GM announced it would lay off more than 14,000 employees in North America, comprising 15% of its workforce and 25% of its executive staff in the region. The company plans to cease production in three assemblies (Lordstown Assembly in Ohio, Detroit-Hamtramck Assembly in Michigan and Oshawa The first GM Corporation in North America 1918 in Canada) and two engine/transmission (White Marsh, Maryland, and Warren, Michigan) plants during 2019. Employees from those plants would also be made redundant.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[66]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="South_America">South America</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=General_Motors&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: South America" data-section="9" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In 2008 the third-largest individual country by sales was <a href="/wiki/General_Motors_do_Brasil" title="General Motors do Brasil">Brazil</a> with some 550,000 GM vehicles sold. In that year Argentina, Colombia, and Venezuela sold another 300,000 GM vehicles, suggesting that the total GM sales in South America (including sales in other South American countries such as Chile, Peru, Ecuador, Bolivia, etc.) in that year were at a similar level to sales in China.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p><p>On April 20, 2017, General Motors announced that the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Venezuela" title="Government of Venezuela">Venezuelan government</a> had seized the General Motors Venezolana plant in <a href="/wiki/Valencia,_Carabobo" title="Valencia, Carabobo">Valencia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[67]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Europe">Europe</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=General_Motors&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Europe" data-section="10" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/General_Motors_Europe" title="General Motors Europe">General Motors Europe</a></div>
<p>Prior to their sale to <a href="/wiki/Groupe_PSA" title="Groupe PSA">Groupe PSA</a> in 2017, <a href="/wiki/Opel" title="Opel">Opel</a> was the main GM brand name in Europe except in the United Kingdom, where Opel's British subsidiary, <a href="/wiki/Vauxhall_Motors" title="Vauxhall Motors">Vauxhall</a>, used its own "Vauxhall" brand name.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Chevrolet" title="Chevrolet">Chevrolet</a> brand was reintroduced in Europe in 2005, selling mostly rebranded <a href="/wiki/Daewoo_Motors" title="Daewoo Motors">Daewoo</a> cars acquired by <a href="/wiki/GM_Korea" title="GM Korea">GM Korea</a>. After having lost approximately $18B over 12 years, GM began phasing out mainstream sales of Chevrolet in Europe in late 2013, and finished by late 2015, to focus on Opel/Vauxhall.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[68]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[69]</a></sup> Chevrolets continue to be sold in <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Independent_States" title="Commonwealth of Independent States">Commonwealth of Independent States</a>, through the <a href="/wiki/GM_Uzbekistan" title="GM Uzbekistan">GM Uzbekistan</a> joint venture.  Chevrolet still has a limited presence in Europe through imports of the <a href="/wiki/Chevrolet_Corvette" title="Chevrolet Corvette">Corvette</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chevrolet_Camaro" title="Chevrolet Camaro">Camaro</a>, while Cadillac maintains a limited presence as well.
</p><p>In 2012, <a href="/wiki/Groupe_PSA" title="Groupe PSA">PSA Peugeot Citroën</a> and General Motors formed an alliance, which involved General Motors acquiring seven percent of the PSA Group.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[70]</a></sup>  The ownership was soon divested on December 13, 2013, generating "gross proceeds of €0.25 billion."<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[71]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[72]</a></sup>  By 2017, Groupe PSA considered taking over Opel from GM, after GM reported a loss of $257 million from its European operations in 2016, the sixteenth consecutive loss-making year for GM in Europe, bringing its total losses in Europe since 2000 to more than US$15 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[73]</a></sup> On March 6, 2017 the sale of Opel and Vauxhall to the PSA Group for $2.3 billion was confirmed.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[74]</a></sup></p>

<td align="right">(8.0)
</td></tr></tbody></table><h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Asia">Asia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=General_Motors&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Asia" data-section="11" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>The company manufactures most of its China market vehicles locally. <a href="/wiki/Shanghai_GM" class="mw-redirect" title="Shanghai GM">Shanghai GM</a>, a joint venture with the Chinese company <a href="/wiki/SAIC_Motor" title="SAIC Motor">SAIC Motor</a>, was created with Canadian Regal in 1990 on March 25, 1997. The Shanghai GM plant was officially opened on December 15, 1998, when the first Chinese-built Buick came off the assembly line. The <a href="/wiki/SAIC-GM-Wuling_Automobile" class="mw-redirect" title="SAIC-GM-Wuling Automobile">SAIC-GM-Wuling Automobile</a> joint-venture is also successfully selling microvans under the <a href="/wiki/SAIC-GM-Wuling_Automobile" class="mw-redirect" title="SAIC-GM-Wuling Automobile">Wuling</a> brand (34 percent owned by GM). Much of General Motors' recent growth has been in the People's Republic of China, where its sales rose 66.9 percent in 2009, selling 1,830,000 vehicles and accounting for 13.4 percent of the market.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[76]</a></sup></p><p><a href="/wiki/Buick" title="Buick">Buick</a> is strong in China from early Introduction by the Canadian Buick sold to the last Emperor of China, later being led by the Buick Regal 1990 subcompact. The <a href="/wiki/Puyi" title="Puyi">last emperor of China</a> owned a Buick.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[77]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Cadillac" title="Cadillac">Cadillac</a> brand was introduced in China in 2004, starting with exports to China. GM pushed the marketing of the <a href="/wiki/Chevrolet" title="Chevrolet">Chevrolet</a> brand in China in the mid-2000s as well. As part of this push, GM transferred <a href="/wiki/Opel_Corsa#Opel_Corsa_B_(1993%E2%80%932000)" title="Opel Corsa">Buick Sail</a> to that brand as an attempt to appeal to Chinese middle-class buyers looking for small and affordable cars.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[78]</a></sup></p><p>In August 2009 the joint venture of FAW GM Light Duty Commercial Vehicle Co Ltd was formed that mainly produces Jiefang light-duty trucks.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[79]</a></sup></p><p>General Motors vehicle sales in China rose 28.8 percent to a record 2,351,610 units in 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[80]</a></sup> GM set up an auto research center as part of a US250 million corporate campus in Shanghai to develop '<a href="/wiki/Hybrid_car" class="mw-redirect" title="Hybrid car">gasoline-hybrid cars</a>, <a href="/wiki/Electric_vehicle" title="Electric vehicle">electric vehicles</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alternative_fuel_vehicle" title="Alternative fuel vehicle">alternative fuels</a>, engines and new technologies'.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[81]</a></sup> The company plans to double its sales from 2010 to about 5 million units in China by 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[82]</a></sup></p><p><a href="/wiki/SAIC-GM-Wuling" title="SAIC-GM-Wuling">SAIC-GM-Wuling</a> established the low-cost <a href="/wiki/Baojun" title="Baojun">Baojun</a> brand to better compete with domestic rivals, <a href="/wiki/Chery_Automobile" class="mw-redirect" title="Chery Automobile">Chery</a>, <a href="/wiki/Geely_Automobile" class="mw-redirect" title="Geely Automobile">Geely</a> and <a href="/wiki/BYD_Auto" title="BYD Auto">BYD</a> for first-time buyers of cars priced around US$10,000. It is estimated that such market in China is about 5 million vehicles a year, larger than the auto market in France and Britain combined. However, some are worried that 'local brands like <a href="/wiki/Baojun" title="Baojun">Baojun</a> could eventually become threats to their parent brands if they compete more against established models over time'. Shanghai-GM-Wuling sold 1.23 million vehicles in 2010, mainly commercial vans and trucks, of which about 700,000 units were a van called Sunshine.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[83]</a></sup></p><p>GM maintains a dealership presence in Japan, called <a href="https://ja.wikipedia.org/wiki/GM%E3%82%B7%E3%83%9C%E3%83%AC%E3%83%BC%E5%BA%97" class="extiw" title="ja:GMシボレー店">GM Chevrolet Shop</a>, previously known as <i>GM Auto World Shop</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[84]</a></sup> Current GM Japan dealerships were either former <a href="/wiki/Saturn_(automobile)" class="mw-redirect" title="Saturn (automobile)">Saturn</a> dealerships or <a href="/wiki/Isuzu" class="mw-redirect" title="Isuzu">Isuzu</a> dealership locations. GM products are also currently sold by the company <a href="/wiki/Yanase_(car_dealership)" title="Yanase (car dealership)">Yanase Co., Ltd.</a> since 1915.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[85]</a></sup></p><p>In August 2011, GM announced plans to reactivate its plant that previously produced rebadged Chevrolet Blazer as Opel as well as Brazilian Blazer, and also build a new plant in <a href="/wiki/Bekasi" title="Bekasi">Bekasi</a>, <a href="/wiki/West_Java" title="West Java">West Java</a>, Indonesia, which would produce 40,000 passenger cars per year for the <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asian" class="mw-redirect" title="Southeast Asian">Southeast Asian</a> market. It is the third plant in Southeast Asia, after the <a href="/wiki/Rayong" title="Rayong">Rayong</a> plant, <a href="/wiki/Thailand" title="Thailand">Thailand</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Hanoi" title="Hanoi">Hanoi</a> plant, <a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">Vietnam</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[86]</a></sup></p><p>In October 2011, the South Korea Free Trade Agreement opened up the South Korean auto market to American made cars.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[87]</a></sup> GM owns (per December 31, 2011) 77.0% of its joint venture in <a href="/wiki/South_Korea" title="South Korea">South Korea</a>, <a href="/wiki/GM_Korea" title="GM Korea">GM Korea</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-GMannualreport2011_15-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GMannualreport2011-15">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>p.96</span></sup></p><p>On March 11, 2013, GM opened a new 190,300 square-foot manufacturing plant in Bekasi, Indonesia.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[88]</a></sup> In February 2015, GM announced they will close the Bekasi plant by the end of June and stop production of the <a href="/wiki/Chevrolet_Sonic" class="mw-redirect" title="Chevrolet Sonic">Sonic</a> in <a href="/wiki/Thailand" title="Thailand">Thailand</a> by mid-year.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[89]</a></sup></p><p>GM announced on May 18, 2017, that it would exit the Indian market, which it had entered for the second time in 1996. The first time was in 1928 when it became the first car maker to manufacture cars in India. GM would, however, continue to manufacture cars from its <a href="/wiki/Talegaon_Dhamdhere" title="Talegaon Dhamdhere">Talegaon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maharashtra" title="Maharashtra">Maharashtra</a> plant for the export market. This plant has a capacity of 1,60,000 units annually. The older Halol, Gujarat plant with a capacity for 50,000 units stopped production on April 28, 2017. It will be sold, with GM in talks with China's <a href="/wiki/SAIC_Motor" title="SAIC Motor">SAIC</a> Motor Corporation Ltd. The India arm's domestic sales for April 2016 – March 2017 declined to 25,823 units from 32,540 the previous year and market share contracted from 1.17 percent to 0.85 percent for the same period. However, exports surged 89 percent during the same period to 70,969 units. GMTC-I, GM's technical center in Bengaluru, India will continue doing its global work. About 400 employees, 8 percent of GM's total Indian work-force, would be affected by the pull-out. Weak product line-up and below par service quality were the reasons for the poor showing by GM in India. It will also affect 10,000 employees working with about 120 Outlets/Dealership of GM in India.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[90]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[91]</a></sup></p><p>In February 2018, comments by CEO Mary Barra that GM's Korean operations' cost structures had "become challenging" fuelled speculation that the company might divest GM Korea, followed by a market exit.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[92]</a></sup> GM is currently negotiating a $2.8 billion investment plan for its Korean operations from the South Korean government, to be dispersed over the next decade. Furthermore, the company approached the Korea Development Bank to participate in a $2.7 billion debt swap issued by its Korean subsidiary.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[93]</a></sup></p><p>According to the South Korean unit of General Motors, its domestic sales for March dropped by 58 percent, which is more than half compared to the past year. In February 2018, General Motors had said to shut down one factory and then decide what lies ahead for the remaining three plants in South Korea during rising losses there. In recent years, the US automaker pulled its Chevy brand from Europe which wedged GM Korea's exports since it was a major market for the Korean firm.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[94]</a></sup></p><p>On February 17, 2020, GM announced it will withdraw from the Thai market and sell its Rayong plant to <a href="/wiki/Great_Wall_Motors" title="Great Wall Motors">Great Wall Motors</a> by the end of the year.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[95]</a></sup></p>

<td align="right">3.3%
</td></tr></tbody></table><h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Africa">Africa</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=General_Motors&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Africa" data-section="12" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>GM has a long history in <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a> which began in the 1920s with the assembly of cars and light pickup trucks for the local market. In the mid of the 1950s, GM withdrew from the Egyptian market. Some years later, the <a href="/wiki/Ghabbour_Group" title="Ghabbour Group">Ghabbour Brothers</a> began to assemble <a href="/wiki/Cadillac" title="Cadillac">Cadillac</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chevrolet" title="Chevrolet">Chevrolet</a> and <a href="/wiki/Buick" title="Buick">Buick</a> models up to the 1990s. Since 1983 GM and <a href="/wiki/Al-Monsour_Automotive" class="mw-redirect" title="Al-Monsour Automotive">Al-Monsour Automotive Company</a> have owned <a href="/wiki/General_Motors_Egypt" title="General Motors Egypt">General Motors Egypt</a>, which is currently the only manufacturer of traditional GM branded vehicles in Egypt.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p><p>In the 1920s <i>Miller Brothers Nigeria</i> was founded as an importer of commercial vehicles of the Bedford brand into the country. In 1949, the company opened its own assembly plant and operated under the name <a href="/wiki/Niger" title="Niger">Niger</a>/<a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigeria</a> Motors. In 1965 the plant and its distribution network was split into different companies and renamed as Federated Motors Industries. In 1991 the company was taken in by a joint venture between <b>General Motors</b> and UACN of <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigeria</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p><p>Another manufacturing base of the GM for the African markets is the <a href="/wiki/Industries_M%C3%A9caniques_Maghr%C3%A9bines" title="Industries Mécaniques Maghrébines">Industries Mécaniques Maghrébines</a> headquartered in <a href="/wiki/Kairouan" title="Kairouan">Kairouan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tunisia" title="Tunisia">Tunisia</a>, which assembles Isuzu and Mazda models for the Maghreb region.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p><p>Formed in 1975, General Motors East Africa (GMEA) was the largest assembler of commercial vehicles in the region exporting them from Kenya to East and Central African countries including <a href="/wiki/Uganda" title="Uganda">Uganda</a>, Tanzania, <a href="/wiki/Malawi" title="Malawi">Malawi</a>, Rwanda and <a href="/wiki/Burundi" title="Burundi">Burundi</a>. Its facility located in <a href="/wiki/Nairobi" title="Nairobi">Nairobi</a> assembled a wide range of Isuzu trucks and buses including the popular Isuzu N-Series versatile light commercial vehicle, TF Series pick-ups and Isuzu bus chassis. In addition to assembly, GMEA also marketed the <a href="/wiki/Chevrolet" title="Chevrolet">Chevrolet</a> products <a href="/wiki/Chevrolet_Spark" title="Chevrolet Spark">Spark</a> and Optra. Selling entire GM's 57.7 per cent stake in General Motors East Africa to Isuzu was announced on February 28, 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[97]</a></sup> After finishing the sale, GMEA was renamed to Isuzu East Africa Limited, effective from August 1, 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[98]</a></sup></p><p>General Motors began operating in South Africa in 1913 through its wholly-owned subsidiary, <a href="/wiki/General_Motors_South_Africa" title="General Motors South Africa">General Motors South Africa</a>. Following the passage of the <a href="/wiki/Comprehensive_Anti-Apartheid_Act" title="Comprehensive Anti-Apartheid Act">Comprehensive Anti-Apartheid Act</a> in 1986, GM was forced to divest from South Africa, and GMSA became the independent Delta Motor Corporation. GM purchased a 49% stake in Delta in 1997 following the end of <a href="/wiki/Apartheid" title="Apartheid">apartheid</a>, and acquired the remaining 51% in 2004, reverting the company to its original name. By 2014 it was targeting the production of 50,000 cars a year but was being hampered by national labor unrest, strikes and protests.<sup id="cite_ref-GMsouthafrica_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GMsouthafrica-100">[99]</a></sup> In May 2017, GM announced that it would exit the South Africa market by the end of 2017 by selling part of the business to Isuzu and look for a buyer for the rest of the business.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[100]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Oceania">Oceania</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=General_Motors&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Oceania" data-section="13" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In New Zealand, GM was represented by locally assembled Chevrolet, Buick, Oldsmobile, Cadillac, and Pontiac vehicles from 1926, and Vauxhall cars from 1931. After World War II, the local production of Chevrolet and Vauxhalls resumed followed by Pontiac again in 1959.
</p><p>In 1954 sales of fully imported <a href="/wiki/Holden" title="Holden">Holden</a> vehicles began. New Zealand assembly of Holdens began in 1957 and by the end of the 1960s Holdens replaced all Chevrolets and Pontiacs (both in 1968), and most Vauxhalls. Opel, Bedford, and Isuzu, vehicles were assembled or imported at different times during the 1970s, 1980s, and 1990s. All local General Motors assembly plants in New Zealand closed by 1990. GM New Zealand was renamed <a href="/wiki/Holden_New_Zealand" title="Holden New Zealand">Holden New Zealand</a> in 1994.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[101]</a></sup></p><p>In Australia, GM has been represented by the Holden brand since 1948. Vauxhall, Chevrolet, and Pontiac vehicles were also assembled in Australia, but production ceased by the end of 1968. 
</p><p>In 2012, GM established Opel as a niche marque in Australia and began to sell Opel branded cars in Australia.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[102]</a></sup> However, less than twelve months later, Opel sales ceased.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[103]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[104]</a></sup></p><p>On December 10, 2013,<sup id="cite_ref-GM-newsrelease_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GM-newsrelease-106">[105]</a></sup> GM announced that Holden would cease manufacturing operations in Australia by the end of 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-OZ-manu-end-2017_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OZ-manu-end-2017-107">[106]</a></sup> Holden's Australian presence now only consists of a national sales company, a parts distribution centre and a global design studio.<sup id="cite_ref-GM-newsrelease_106-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GM-newsrelease-106">[105]</a></sup> Holdens are now sourced from GM's Korean and North American operations, and PSA (Opel). 
</p><p>On February 17, 2020, GM announced that it would exit Australian, New Zealand, and Thailand markets, and confirmed that the Holden badge would cease to exist by 2021. The global design center and <a href="/wiki/General_Motors_Proving_Grounds#Lang_Lang_Proving_Ground" title="General Motors Proving Grounds">Lang Lang</a> (Victoria) test track are set to be closed, with the remaining 200 staff catering for warranty-related claims for up to 10 years. Despite its announcement, GM will continue to have some presence in Australia, as they plan to export some Chevrolet, Cadillac, and GMC vehicles through a new  entity called General Motors Specialty Vehicles, as plans are still on track to bring American-built brands to the region, which was announced before Holden's shutdown.<sup id="cite_ref-caradvice-holden-axed_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-caradvice-holden-axed-108">[107]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[108]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(5)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Motorsports">Motorsports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=General_Motors&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Motorsports" data-section="14" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-5 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-5">
<table class="box-Unreferenced_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=General_Motors&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>.
