<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Nicola_Larini_2009_WTCC_Marrakech.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Nicola_Larini_2009_WTCC_Marrakech.jpg/220px-Nicola_Larini_2009_WTCC_Marrakech.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="127" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="1869" data-file-height="1080"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 127px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Nicola_Larini_2009_WTCC_Marrakech.jpg/220px-Nicola_Larini_2009_WTCC_Marrakech.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="127" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Nicola_Larini_2009_WTCC_Marrakech.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Chevrolet Cruze in the WTCC</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Corvette_4_LS.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Corvette_4_LS.jpg/220px-Corvette_4_LS.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="2560" data-file-height="1920"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 165px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Corvette_4_LS.jpg/220px-Corvette_4_LS.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="165" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Corvette_4_LS.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Corvette Racing Team in the <a href="/wiki/American_Le_Mans_Series" title="American Le Mans Series">American Le Mans Series</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Holden_VE_Commodore_of_James_Courtney_2012.JPG" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Holden_VE_Commodore_of_James_Courtney_2012.JPG/220px-Holden_VE_Commodore_of_James_Courtney_2012.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="2504" data-file-height="1413"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 124px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Holden_VE_Commodore_of_James_Courtney_2012.JPG/220px-Holden_VE_Commodore_of_James_Courtney_2012.JPG" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="124" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Holden_VE_Commodore_of_James_Courtney_2012.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Holden_VE_Commodore" class="mw-redirect" title="Holden VE Commodore">Holden VE Commodore</a> of <a href="/wiki/James_Courtney" title="James Courtney">James Courtney</a> (<a href="/wiki/Holden_Racing_Team" class="mw-redirect" title="Holden Racing Team">Holden Racing Team</a>) at the <a href="/wiki/2012_Clipsal_500_Adelaide" class="mw-redirect" title="2012 Clipsal 500 Adelaide">2012 Clipsal 500 Adelaide</a></div></div></div>
<p>GM has participated over the years in the <a href="/wiki/World_Touring_Car_Championship" title="World Touring Car Championship">World Touring Car Championship</a> (WTCC), <a href="/wiki/24_Hours_of_Le_Mans" title="24 Hours of Le Mans">24 Hours of Le Mans</a>, <a href="/wiki/NASCAR" title="NASCAR">NASCAR</a>, <a href="/wiki/SCCA" class="mw-redirect" title="SCCA">SCCA</a>, <a href="/wiki/Supercars_Championship" title="Supercars Championship">Supercars Championship</a>, and many other world venues.
</p><p>GM's engines were highly successful in the <a href="/wiki/Indy_Racing_League" class="mw-redirect" title="Indy Racing League">Indy Racing League</a> (IRL) throughout the 1990s, winning many races in the small <a href="/wiki/V8_engine" title="V8 engine">V-8</a> class. GM has also done much work in the <a href="/wiki/Development_of_electronics_for_GM_auto_racing" title="Development of electronics for GM auto racing">development of electronics for GM auto racing</a>. An unmodified Aurora V-8 in the Aerotech, captured 47 world records, including the record for speed endurance in the Motorsports Hall of Fame of America. Recently, the <a href="/wiki/Cadillac_V-Series" class="mw-redirect" title="Cadillac V-Series">Cadillac V-Series</a> has entered motorsports racing.
</p><p>GM has also used many cars in the American racing series <a href="/wiki/NASCAR" title="NASCAR">NASCAR</a>. Currently the <a href="/wiki/Chevrolet_Camaro" title="Chevrolet Camaro">Chevrolet Camaro ZL1</a> is the only entry in the series, but in the past the <a href="/wiki/Pontiac_Grand_Prix" title="Pontiac Grand Prix">Pontiac Grand Prix</a>, <a href="/wiki/Buick_Regal" title="Buick Regal">Buick Regal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oldsmobile_Cutlass" title="Oldsmobile Cutlass">Oldsmobile Cutlass</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chevrolet_Lumina" title="Chevrolet Lumina">Chevrolet Lumina</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chevrolet_Malibu" title="Chevrolet Malibu">Chevrolet Malibu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chevrolet_Monte_Carlo" title="Chevrolet Monte Carlo">Chevrolet Monte Carlo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chevrolet_Impala" title="Chevrolet Impala">Chevrolet Impala</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Chevrolet_SS" class="mw-redirect" title="Chevrolet SS">Chevrolet SS</a> were also used. GM has won a total of 40 <a href="/wiki/NASCAR_Cup_Series" title="NASCAR Cup Series">NASCAR Cup Series</a> <a href="/wiki/List_of_NASCAR_Manufacturers%27_champions" title="List of NASCAR Manufacturers' champions">manufacturer's championships</a>, including 34 with Chevrolet, the most of any make in NASCAR history, 3 with Oldsmobile, 2 with Buick, and 1 with Pontiac. GM leads all other automobile manufacturers in races won in NASCAR's premier series at 1,011. Chevrolet leads individual makes with 677 wins.
</p><p>In Australia, there is the <a href="/wiki/Supercars_Championship" title="Supercars Championship">Supercars Championship</a> which is battled out by the two main rivals of (GM) <a href="/wiki/Holden" title="Holden">Holden</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ford_Motor_Company" title="Ford Motor Company">Ford</a>. The current <a href="/wiki/Holden" title="Holden">Holden</a> Racing Team cars are based on the <a href="/wiki/Holden_Commodore" title="Holden Commodore">Holden Commodore</a> and run a 5.0-litre V8-cylinder engine producing 635 bhp (474 kW). These cars have a top speed of 298 km/h (185 mph) and run 0–100 km/h in 3.8 seconds. The <a href="/wiki/Holden_Racing_Team" class="mw-redirect" title="Holden Racing Team">Holden Racing Team</a> is Australia's most successful team in Australian touring car history. In 2006 and 2007, the drivers' championship was won by the very closely linked (now defunct) <a href="/wiki/HSV_Dealer_Team" title="HSV Dealer Team">HSV Dealer Team</a>. With Holden's demise in 2020, GM is expected to make the exported Chevrolet Camaro the successor-in-line to the Holden Commodore once existing deals are completed.
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(6)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Research_and_development">Research and development</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=General_Motors&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Research and development" data-section="15" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-6 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-6">
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/General_Motors_Technical_Center" title="General Motors Technical Center">General Motors Technical Center</a> and <a href="/wiki/General_Motors_Proving_Grounds" title="General Motors Proving Grounds">General Motors Proving Grounds</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Research_and_development" title="Research and development">Research and development</a> (R&amp;D) at General Motors began organically as the continuation of such R&amp;D as the various divisions (e.g., Cadillac, Buick, Olds, Oakland) were already doing for themselves before the merger. Its character was entirely empirical; it was whatever key people in each company had been competent enough to organize and pursue.
<a href="/wiki/Robert_McLaughlin_(industrialist)" title="Robert McLaughlin (industrialist)">R. S. McLaughlin</a>'s Carriage Company in 1876 was designing and inventing Carriage Gear. The <a href="/wiki/McLaughlin_Motor_Car_Company" title="McLaughlin Motor Car Company">McLaughlin Companies</a> became General Motors of Canada Limited.
<a href="/wiki/Charles_F._Kettering" title="Charles F. Kettering">Charles F. Kettering</a>'s Dayton Engineering Laboratories Company (Delco), at <a href="/wiki/Dayton,_Ohio" title="Dayton, Ohio">Dayton, Ohio</a>, was still an independent firm at this time. Its work was well known to GM central management through its relationship as a supplier and consultancy to Cadillac and Buick.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p><p>In 1916, Durant organized the United Motors Corporation as an amalgamation of parts suppliers, supplying GM and other OEMs but independent of GM.<sup id="cite_ref-Sloan1964pp24,97_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sloan1964pp24,97-110">[109]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Alfred_P._Sloan" title="Alfred P. Sloan">Alfred P. Sloan</a>, head of the newly acquired <a href="/wiki/Hyatt_Roller_Bearing_Corporation" class="mw-redirect" title="Hyatt Roller Bearing Corporation">Hyatt Roller Bearing Corporation</a>, became United Motors' CEO. United Motors acquired Delco, and Kettering began his association with Sloan. United Motors also acquired at this time the original Remy corporation<sup id="cite_ref-Sloan1964pp24,97_110-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sloan1964pp24,97-110">[109]</a></sup> (called the Remy Electric Company), a competitor of Delco. In 1918 General Motors bought United Motors.<sup id="cite_ref-Sloan1964pp24,97_110-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sloan1964pp24,97-110">[109]</a></sup> Various entities grew out of the original Delco and Remy, including the Dayton Metal Products Corporation, the General Motors Research Corporation, the Delco Division and Remy Electric Division of GM, Delco Remy (now <a href="/wiki/Remy_International,_Inc." class="mw-redirect" title="Remy International, Inc.">Remy International, Inc.</a>), <a href="/wiki/ACDelco" title="ACDelco">ACDelco</a>, <a href="/wiki/Delco_Electronics" title="Delco Electronics">Delco Electronics</a>, and others. Today's main successor corporation is <a href="/wiki/Delphi_Automotive" class="mw-redirect" title="Delphi Automotive">Delphi Automotive</a>, which nowadays is an independent parent corporation.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p><p>The General Motors Research Corporation, at Dayton under Kettering, became a true automotive research center. During the next few decades it led the development of:
</p>
<ul><li>Many electrical-appliance features for cars and trucks</li>
<li>In 1911, Charles F. Kettering, with Henry M. Leland, of Dayton Engineering Laboratories Company (DELCO) invented and filed U.S. Patent 1,150,523 for the <a href="/wiki/Starter_(engine)" title="Starter (engine)">first electric starter</a> in America.</li>
<li>In 1921, General Motors patented the use of <a href="/wiki/Tetraethyllead" title="Tetraethyllead">Tetraethyllead</a> as an antiknock agent leading to the development of higher compression engines resulting in more power and efficiency even though much later it was realized that lead in gasoline was harmful to various biological organisms including humans.<sup id="cite_ref-Kitman_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kitman-111">[110]</a></sup></li>
<li>In 1937, Jominy &amp; Boegehold<sup id="cite_ref-W.E._Jominy_1938,_p_574-606_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-W.E._Jominy_1938,_p_574-606-112">[111]</a></sup> of GM invented the Jominy end-quench test for <a href="/wiki/Hardenability" title="Hardenability">hardenability</a> of carbon steel, a breakthrough in <a href="/wiki/Heat_treating" title="Heat treating">heat treating</a> still in use today as <a href="/wiki/ASTM" class="mw-redirect" title="ASTM">ASTM</a> A255.<sup id="cite_ref-ASTM_A255-10_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ASTM_A255-10-113">[112]</a></sup></li>
<li>In 1939, GM introduced the world's first automatic transmission the Hydra-matic for the 1940 Oldsmobile and would be adopted by the auto industry later.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[113]</a></sup></li>
<li>In 1962, GM introduced the first turbo charged engine in the world for a car in the Oldsmobile Cutlass Turbo-Jetfire.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[114]</a></sup></li>
<li>In 1971, the <a href="/wiki/Lunar_Roving_Vehicle" title="Lunar Roving Vehicle">Lunar Rover</a>, a partnership between GM's Delco Defense Electronics Division and <a href="/wiki/Boeing" title="Boeing">Boeing</a> traversed the surface of the Moon.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[115]</a></sup></li>
<li>In 1972, GM produced the first rear wheel Anti-lock brake system in the world for two of their cars: the Toronado and Eldorado.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[116]</a></sup></li>
<li>In 1984, Robert Lee<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[117]</a></sup> of GM invented the <a href="/wiki/Neodymium_magnet" title="Neodymium magnet">Fe<sub>14</sub>Nd<sub>2</sub>B permanent magnet</a>, fabricated by rapid solidification.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Dichlorodifluoromethane" title="Dichlorodifluoromethane">Dichlorodifluoromethane</a> refrigerant for <a href="/wiki/HVAC" class="mw-redirect" title="HVAC">HVAC</a> and <a href="/wiki/Refrigeration" title="Refrigeration">refrigeration</a> applications (Freon, R-12; recognized today as a bad idea environmentally [being a <a href="/wiki/Chlorofluorocarbon" title="Chlorofluorocarbon">chlorofluorocarbon</a> (CFC)], but a technological wonder of its day)</li>
<li>Commercially practical <a href="/wiki/Two-stroke_diesel_engine" title="Two-stroke diesel engine">two-stroke diesel engines</a></li>
<li>Better transmissions for track-laying vehicles</li>
<li>Many other advancements</li></ul><p>Although GM R&amp;D (as it is known in colloquial shorthand) began as an organization largely built around one man (Kettering), it eventually evolved into a more modern organization whose path is shaped by individuals but not dominated entirely by any of them. World War II was a turning point wherein military affairs, after mingling with the technologies of applied science for some 80 years, first started to become fundamentally reinvented by them. Civilian life, too, changed in this direction. By the 1950s, corporations such as GM and many others were facing a new era of R&amp;D, different from earlier ones. Less about genius inventors and individual inventions, and more about organizational progress and integrated systems, it raised new questions about where the <a href="/wiki/Capital_(economics)" title="Capital (economics)">capital</a> for R&amp;D would come from in an era of limitless demand for R&amp;D (although not necessarily for production). <a href="/wiki/Alfred_P._Sloan" title="Alfred P. Sloan">Alfred Sloan</a>, longtime CEO of GM (1920s to 1960s), discussed in his memoir (also considered a seminal management treatise) the relationships between government, academia, and private industry in the areas of basic science and applied science, in light of this new era.<sup id="cite_ref-Sloan1964pp249-252_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sloan1964pp249-252-119">[118]</a></sup> The views he laid out reflected (and influenced) wide consensus on these relationships that persists largely to today.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p><p>Today, GM R&amp;D, headquartered in <a href="/wiki/Warren,_Michigan" title="Warren, Michigan">Warren, Michigan</a>, is a network of six laboratories, six science offices, and collaborative relationships in over twelve countries including working relationships with universities, government groups, suppliers, and other partners from across the globe.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[119]</a></sup></p><p>On September 7, 2014, at the Intelligent Transport Systems World Congress in Detroit GM disclosed it would be introducing auto-pilot features into certain 2017 models of its cars, which would go on sale in 2016. The "super cruise" or vehicle-to-vehicle V2V technology is likely to be first introduced to the Cadillac range, enabling drivers to switch in and out of semi-automated mode.<sup id="cite_ref-GMautomated_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GMautomated-121">[120]</a></sup> In December 2016, General Motors announced it would begin testing self-driving vehicles on public roads in Michigan after Gov. Rick Snyder signed a package of bills legalizing the operation of autonomous vehicles.<sup id="cite_ref-Fortune_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fortune-122">[121]</a></sup></p><p>In March 2016, General Motors bought Cruise Automation, a San Francisco self-driving vehicle start-up, to develop self-driving cars that could be used in ride-sharing fleets.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[122]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[123]</a></sup></p><p>In October 2017, General Motors acquired Strobe, a solid state <a href="/wiki/LIDAR" class="mw-redirect" title="LIDAR">LIDAR</a> company. Strobe's prototypes produce brief "chirps" of frequency-modulated (FM) laser light, where the frequency within each chirp varies linearly. Measuring the phase and frequency of the echoing chirp allows the system to directly measure both the distance and the velocity of objects in the road ahead. Strobe, Cruise and GM will work together to develop the technology for future self-driving cars.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[124]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[125]</a></sup></p><p>In November 2017 Two self-driving Chevy Bolt EV cars were seen during a media event by Cruise Automation, GM's <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_car" class="mw-redirect" title="Autonomous car">autonomous car</a> unit, in San Francisco, California, U.S. The automaker is already operating self-driving Chevy Bolts in San Francisco as part of a beta test run by the company's subsidiary.
</p><p>In October 2018, <a href="/wiki/Honda" title="Honda">Honda</a> announced the investment of $2.75 billion in GM's self-driving car unit. The firm announced an initial investment of $275 million initially, followed by $2 billion within the year.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[126]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[127]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[128]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(7)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Small_car_sales">Small car sales</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=General_Motors&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Small car sales" data-section="16" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-7 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-7">
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Chevrolet_Aveo_RS_concept_front.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Chevrolet_Aveo_RS_concept_front.jpg/220px-Chevrolet_Aveo_RS_concept_front.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="154" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="2332" data-file-height="1628"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 154px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Chevrolet_Aveo_RS_concept_front.jpg/220px-Chevrolet_Aveo_RS_concept_front.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="154" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Chevrolet_Aveo_RS_concept_front.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Chevrolet Aveo Concept</div></div></div>
<p>From the 1920s onward, General Motors always maintained an internal dialog about what its economy-car and small-car policies should be.<sup id="cite_ref-Sloan1964pp313-339_130-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sloan1964pp313-339-130">[129]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Sloan1964pp440-442_131-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sloan1964pp440-442-131">[130]</a></sup> The economy and size considerations often naturally overlapped, although a strong distinction was always drawn in the 20th century between policies for the U.S. market and policies for other markets. Economy (in some form) always had good demand anywhere, but its definition in the U.S. was long considered different from that in other markets. In this view, "economy" in the U.S. did not mean "small" in the sense of what qualified as "small" outside the U.S. The policy discussion often focused on topics like the higher demand for truly small cars in non-U.S. markets than in the U.S., and whether it made more sense to import a car into a certain country or to build it domestically within that country, either as some variant of <a href="/wiki/Knock-down_kit" title="Knock-down kit">knockdown</a> or with truly extensive domestic sourcing.<sup id="cite_ref-Sloan1964pp313-339_130-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sloan1964pp313-339-130">[129]</a></sup> GM's acquisitions of Vauxhall Motors Ltd (UK, 1925)<sup id="cite_ref-Sloan1964pp313-339_130-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sloan1964pp313-339-130">[129]</a></sup> and Adam Opel AG (Germany, 1929),<sup id="cite_ref-Sloan1964pp313-339_130-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sloan1964pp313-339-130">[129]</a></sup> rather than starting new domestic companies to compete against them, were based on analyses that convinced GM managers that acquiring an existing domestic manufacturer was a better business decision.<sup id="cite_ref-Sloan1964pp313-339_130-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sloan1964pp313-339-130">[129]</a></sup></p><p>Although GM since the 1920s has always offered economy models in the U.S. market (relative to that market's definition in any given decade) and had done research and development in the 1940s and 1950s in preparation for any potential rise of strong demand for truly small cars in the U.S. market,<sup id="cite_ref-Sloan1964pp440-442_131-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sloan1964pp440-442-131">[130]</a></sup> it has also been criticized over the decades for not doing enough to promote fuel efficiency in the U.S. market in the 1970s through 1990s. GM's response has been that it has always responded to market demands and that most Americans, despite anything they said to the contrary, did not actually demand (at purchasing-decision time) small size or fuel efficiency in their vehicles to any great or lasting extent. Although some U.S. consumers flocked temporarily to the ideal of fuel economy whenever fuel supply crises arose (such as 1973 and 1979), they flocked equally enthusiastically to SUVs when cheap fuel of the 1980s and 1990s temporarily shielded them from any downside to these choices.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p><p>Since the return of high fuel prices in the 2000s and 2010s, GM's interest in truly small-car programs for the U.S. market has been renewed. As part of General Motors Company development, GM revived one of its idled U.S. factories for the production of a small car in <a href="/wiki/Orion,_Michigan" class="mw-redirect" title="Orion, Michigan">Orion, Michigan</a>, with the creation of 1,200 American jobs. This will be the first time that GM produced a <a href="/wiki/Sub_compact_car" class="mw-redirect" title="Sub compact car">sub compact car</a> in the United States since the <a href="/wiki/Chevrolet_Chevette" title="Chevrolet Chevette">Chevrolet Chevette</a> ended production in 1986. This retooled plant will be capable of building 160,000 cars annually, including both small and compact vehicles. Production started in late 2011 with the <a href="/wiki/Chevrolet_Sonic" class="mw-redirect" title="Chevrolet Sonic">Chevrolet Sonic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[131]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(8)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Environmental_initiatives">Environmental initiatives</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=General_Motors&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Environmental initiatives" data-section="17" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-8 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-8">
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:DCA_06_2012_Chevy_Volt_4035.JPG" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/DCA_06_2012_Chevy_Volt_4035.JPG/220px-DCA_06_2012_Chevy_Volt_4035.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="1950" data-file-height="1300"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 147px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/DCA_06_2012_Chevy_Volt_4035.JPG/220px-DCA_06_2012_Chevy_Volt_4035.JPG" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="147" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:DCA_06_2012_Chevy_Volt_4035.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Chevrolet_Volt" title="Chevrolet Volt">Chevrolet Volt</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Series_plug-in_hybrid" class="mw-redirect" title="Series plug-in hybrid">series plug-in hybrid</a>, ranks as the U.S. all-time top-selling <a href="/wiki/Plug-in_electric_car" class="mw-redirect" title="Plug-in electric car">plug-in electric car</a> with 148,556 units sold through October 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-TopUS102018_133-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TopUS102018-133">[132]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>General Motors has published principles regarding the environment and maintains an extensive website to inform the public. In 2008, General Motors committed to engineering half of its manufacturing plants to be landfill-free. In order to achieve its landfill-free status, production waste is recycled or reused in the manufacturing process.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[133]</a></sup></p><p><a href="/wiki/List_of_rooftop_photovoltaic_installations" title="List of rooftop photovoltaic installations">The world's largest rooftop solar power installation</a> was installed at General Motors Spanish Zaragoza Manufacturing Plant in late 2008. The Zaragoza solar installation has about 2,000,000 square feet (190,000 m<sup>2</sup>) of roof at the plant and contains about 85,000 solar panels. The installation was created, owned and operated by Veolia Environment and Clairvoyant Energy, who lease the rooftop area from General Motors.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[134]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[135]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[136]</a></sup> In 2011, General Motors also invested $7.5 million in solar-panel provider Sunlogics, which will install solar panels on GM facilities.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[137]</a></sup></p><p>GM has long worked on <a href="/wiki/Alternative_fuel_vehicle" title="Alternative fuel vehicle">alternative-technology vehicles</a>, and has led the industry with ethanol-burning <a href="/wiki/Flexible-fuel_vehicle" title="Flexible-fuel vehicle">flexible-fuel vehicles</a> that can run on either <a href="/wiki/E85" title="E85">E85</a> (ethanol) or gasoline. The company was the first to use <a href="/wiki/Turbocharger" title="Turbocharger">turbochargers</a> and was an early proponent of <a href="/wiki/V6_engine" title="V6 engine">V6 engines</a> in the 1960s, but quickly lost interest as <a href="/wiki/Muscle_car" title="Muscle car">muscle car</a> popularity increased. They demonstrated<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[138]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Gas_turbine" title="Gas turbine">gas turbine</a> vehicles powered by <a href="/wiki/Kerosene" title="Kerosene">kerosene</a>, an area of interest throughout the industry, but abandoned the alternative engine configuration in view of the <a href="/wiki/1973_oil_crisis" title="1973 oil crisis">1973 oil crisis</a>. In the 1970s and 1980s, GM pushed the benefits of <a href="/wiki/Diesel_engine" title="Diesel engine">diesel engines</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cylinder_deactivation" class="mw-redirect" title="Cylinder deactivation">cylinder deactivation</a> technologies with disastrous results due to poor durability in the <a href="/wiki/Oldsmobile" title="Oldsmobile">Oldsmobile</a> diesels and drivability issues in the <a href="/wiki/Cadillac" title="Cadillac">Cadillac</a> V8-6-4 variable-cylinder engines. In 1987, GM, in conjunction with <a href="/wiki/AeroVironment" title="AeroVironment">AeroVironment</a>, built the <a href="/wiki/Sunraycer" title="Sunraycer">Sunraycer</a>, which won the inaugural <a href="/wiki/World_Solar_Challenge" title="World Solar Challenge">World Solar Challenge</a> and was a showcase of advanced technology. Much of the technology from Sunraycer found its way into the Impact prototype electric vehicle (also built by Aerovironment) and was the predecessor to the <a href="/wiki/General_Motors_EV1" title="General Motors EV1">General Motors EV1</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[139]</a></sup></p><p>GM supported a compromise version of the <a href="/wiki/Corporate_Average_Fuel_Economy" class="mw-redirect" title="Corporate Average Fuel Economy">Corporate Average Fuel Economy</a> (CAFE) standard increase from 27 to 35 mpg<sub>‑US</sub> (8.7 to 6.7 L/100 km; 32 to 42 mpg<sub>‑imp</sub>), the first such increase in over 20 years.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[140]</a></sup> GM hinted that they will not introduce more Volt-based plug-in hybrids.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[141]</a></sup></p><p>The company has publicly announced that it is committed to invest heavily in <a href="/wiki/Electric_car" title="Electric car">electric cars</a>. In October 2017, GM's executive vice president of global development, <a href="/wiki/Mark_Reuss" title="Mark Reuss">Mark Reuss</a>, announced that GM's vehicle lineup would feature 20 electric car models by 2023.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[142]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[143]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Hybrid_electric_vehicles">Hybrid electric vehicles</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=General_Motors&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Hybrid electric vehicles" data-section="18" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Chevrolet_Tahoe_hybrid_MLB_All_Star_Game_edition_at_67_St_NYC.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Chevrolet_Tahoe_hybrid_MLB_All_Star_Game_edition_at_67_St_NYC.jpg/220px-Chevrolet_Tahoe_hybrid_MLB_All_Star_Game_edition_at_67_St_NYC.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 165px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Chevrolet_Tahoe_hybrid_MLB_All_Star_Game_edition_at_67_St_NYC.jpg/220px-Chevrolet_Tahoe_hybrid_MLB_All_Star_Game_edition_at_67_St_NYC.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="165" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Chevrolet_Tahoe_hybrid_MLB_All_Star_Game_edition_at_67_St_NYC.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Chevrolet Tahoe Hybrid</div></div></div>
<p>In May 2004, GM delivered the world's first full-sized hybrid pickups, the 1/2-ton Silverado/Sierra. These <a href="/wiki/Mild_hybrid" title="Mild hybrid">mild hybrids</a> did not use electrical energy for propulsion, like GM's later designs. In 2005, the <a href="/wiki/Opel_Astra" title="Opel Astra">Opel Astra</a> <a href="/wiki/Diesel_engine" title="Diesel engine">diesel</a> <a href="/wiki/Hybrid_vehicle" title="Hybrid vehicle">Hybrid</a> <a href="/wiki/Concept_vehicle" class="mw-redirect" title="Concept vehicle">concept vehicle</a> was introduced. The 2006 <a href="/wiki/Saturn_Vue#Green_Line" title="Saturn Vue">Saturn Vue Green Line</a> was the first hybrid passenger vehicle from GM and is also a mild design. GM has hinted at new hybrid technologies to be employed that will be optimized for higher speeds in freeway driving.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[144]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p><p>GM offered the <a href="/wiki/2-mode_hybrid" class="mw-redirect" title="2-mode hybrid">2-mode hybrid</a> system in the 2008–2013 Chevrolet Tahoe/GMC Yukon/Cadillac Escalade, and 2009–2013 GM 1/2 half-ton pickups.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">[145]</a></sup> This hybrid technology, co-developed with DaimlerChrysler and BMW, was first used by GM in a diesel-electric hybrid powertrain (manufactured by <a href="/wiki/Allison_Transmission" title="Allison Transmission">Allison Transmission</a>) for transit buses, starting in 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">[146]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Extended-Range_Electric_Vehicle">Extended-Range Electric Vehicle</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=General_Motors&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Extended-Range Electric Vehicle" data-section="19" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Chevrolet_Volt_WAS_2017_1533.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Chevrolet_Volt_WAS_2017_1533.jpg/220px-Chevrolet_Volt_WAS_2017_1533.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="116" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="2843" data-file-height="1500"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 116px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Chevrolet_Volt_WAS_2017_1533.jpg/220px-Chevrolet_Volt_WAS_2017_1533.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="116" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Chevrolet_Volt_WAS_2017_1533.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Chevrolet_Volt_(second_generation)" title="Chevrolet Volt (second generation)">Second generation Chevrolet Volt</a></div></div></div>
<p>Within the framework of its vehicle electrification strategy,<sup id="cite_ref-VDI_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-VDI-148">[147]</a></sup> GM introduced the <a href="/wiki/Chevrolet_Volt" title="Chevrolet Volt">Chevrolet Volt</a> in 2010 as an Extended-Range Electric Vehicle (EREV), an electric vehicle with back-up generators powered by gasoline, or <a href="/wiki/Series_plug-in_hybrid" class="mw-redirect" title="Series plug-in hybrid">series plug-in hybrid</a>. The production Chevrolet Volt was available in late 2010 as a 2011 model with limited availability.<sup id="cite_ref-RSC_149-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RSC-149">[148]</a></sup> GM delivered the first Volt during December 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">[149]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Chevrolet_Volt_(second_generation)" title="Chevrolet Volt (second generation)">second-generation Volt</a> was launched in the U.S. and Canada in October 2015. The second generation has an upgraded drivetrain and improved battery system that increased the <a href="/wiki/All-electric_range" title="All-electric range">all-electric range</a> to 53 miles (85 km) from 38 miles (61 km).<sup id="cite_ref-2016Volt_151-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2016Volt-151">[150]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Canada2015_152-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Canada2015-152">[151]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-EPAVolt2016_153-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EPAVolt2016-153">[152]</a></sup>  In November 2018, GM announced it would cease Volt production in March 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-End2019_154-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-End2019-154">[153]</a></sup></p><p>As of October 2018<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=General_Motors&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, global Volt/Ampera family sales totaled about 177,000 units since its inception in December 2010,<sup id="cite_ref-Top5Global102018_155-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Top5Global102018-155">[154]</a></sup> including over 10,000 Opel/Vauxhall Amperas sold in Europe up to December 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-LeafBest250K_156-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LeafBest250K-156">[155]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Top10Global062016_157-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Top10Global062016-157">[156]</a></sup> The Volt family of vehicles ranked as the world's all-time top-selling <a href="/wiki/Plug-in_hybrid" title="Plug-in hybrid">plug-in hybrid</a> as of September 2018<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=General_Motors&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, and it is also the third best selling <a href="/wiki/Plug-in_electric_car" class="mw-redirect" title="Plug-in electric car">plug-in electric car</a> in history after the <a href="/wiki/Nissan_Leaf" title="Nissan Leaf">Nissan Leaf</a> (375,000) and the <a href="/wiki/Tesla_Model_S" title="Tesla Model S">Tesla Model S</a> (253,000), as of October 2018<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=General_Motors&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> .<sup id="cite_ref-Top5Global102018_155-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Top5Global102018-155">[154]</a></sup> The Chevrolet Volt is also the U.S. all-time top-selling <a href="/wiki/Plug-in_electric_car" class="mw-redirect" title="Plug-in electric car">plug-in electric car</a> with 148,556 units delivered through October 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-TopUS102018_133-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TopUS102018-133">[132]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="All-electric_vehicles">All-electric vehicles</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=General_Motors&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: All-electric vehicles" data-section="20" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:EV1_(6).jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/EV1_%286%29.jpg/220px-EV1_%286%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="158" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="723" data-file-height="520"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 158px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/EV1_%286%29.jpg/220px-EV1_%286%29.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="158" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:EV1_(6).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Electric_car" title="Electric car">all-electric</a> <a href="/wiki/General_Motors_EV1" title="General Motors EV1">General Motors EV1</a> was introduced in California in 1996</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Chevrolet_Bolt_EV_SAO_2016_8894.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Chevrolet_Bolt_EV_SAO_2016_8894.jpg/220px-Chevrolet_Bolt_EV_SAO_2016_8894.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="2400" data-file-height="1600"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 147px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Chevrolet_Bolt_EV_SAO_2016_8894.jpg/220px-Chevrolet_Bolt_EV_SAO_2016_8894.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="147" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Chevrolet_Bolt_EV_SAO_2016_8894.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Chevrolet_Bolt_EV" class="mw-redirect" title="Chevrolet Bolt EV">Chevrolet Bolt EV</a> was released in California by late 2016</div></div></div>
<p>General Motors was the first company (in the modern era) to release an all-electric automobile.<sup id="cite_ref-VDI_148-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-VDI-148">[147]</a></sup> In 1990, GM debuted the "Impact" concept car at the Los Angeles Auto Show. It was the first car with zero-emissions marketed in the US in over three decades. The Impact was eventually produced as the <a href="/wiki/EV1" class="mw-redirect" title="EV1">EV1</a> for the 1996 model year. It was available through dealers located in only a few regions (e.g., California, Arizona, Georgia). Vehicles were leased, rather than sold, to individuals. In 1999 GM decided to cease production of the vehicles. When the individual leases had expired, they declined to renew the leases or allow the lessors to purchase them. All of the EV1s were eventually returned to General Motors and, with the exception of a few which were donated to museums, all were destroyed. The documentary film <i><a href="/wiki/Who_Killed_the_Electric_Car%3F" title="Who Killed the Electric Car?">Who Killed the Electric Car?</a></i> covered the EV1 story.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">[157]</a></sup></p><p>The EV1's cancellation had disappointed supporters of electric vehicles. In 2010, GM debuted the <a href="/wiki/Chevrolet_Volt" title="Chevrolet Volt">Chevrolet Volt</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Plug-in_hybrid_electric_vehicle" class="mw-redirect" title="Plug-in hybrid electric vehicle">plug-in hybrid electric vehicle</a> with back-up generators powered by gasoline (<a href="/wiki/Range_extender_(vehicle)" class="mw-redirect" title="Range extender (vehicle)">range-extended electric vehicle</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-R1_159-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-R1-159">[158]</a></sup> General Motors has announced that it is building a prototype two-seat electric vehicle with <a href="/wiki/Segway_Inc." title="Segway Inc.">Segway</a>. An early prototype of the Personal Urban Mobility and Accessibility vehicle—dubbed <a href="/wiki/Personal_Urban_Mobility_and_Accessibility" title="Personal Urban Mobility and Accessibility">Project P.U.M.A.</a> – was presented in New York at the 2009 <a href="/wiki/New_York_International_Auto_Show" title="New York International Auto Show">New York International Auto Show</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">[159]</a></sup></p><p>In October 2011, General Motors announced the production of the <a href="/wiki/Chevrolet_Spark_EV" class="mw-redirect" title="Chevrolet Spark EV">Chevrolet Spark EV</a>, an <a href="/wiki/All-electric_car" class="mw-redirect" title="All-electric car">all-electric</a> version of the third generation <a href="/wiki/Chevrolet_Spark" title="Chevrolet Spark">Chevrolet Spark</a>, with availability limited to select U.S. and global markets. In October 2012, GM Korea announced it will start making and selling the Spark EV domestically in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">[160]</a></sup> The production version was unveiled at the 2012 <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Auto_Show" class="mw-redirect" title="Los Angeles Auto Show">Los Angeles Auto Show</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT112812_162-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT112812-162">[161]</a></sup> Within the framework of GM's vehicle electrification strategy,<sup id="cite_ref-VDI_148-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-VDI-148">[147]</a></sup> the Spark EV is the first all-electric passenger car marketed by General Motors in the U.S. since the <a href="/wiki/General_Motors_EV1" title="General Motors EV1">EV1</a> was discontinued in 1999.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT101211_163-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT101211-163">[162]</a></sup> The Spark EV was released in the U.S. in selected markets in California and Oregon in June 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-EVreleased_164-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EVreleased-164">[163]</a></sup> Retail sales began in South Korea in October 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">[164]</a></sup> GM also plans to sell the Spark EV in limited quantities in Canada and select European markets.<sup id="cite_ref-GCC112712_166-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GCC112712-166">[165]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">[166]</a></sup></p><p>GM began production of the <a href="/wiki/Chevrolet_Bolt_EV" class="mw-redirect" title="Chevrolet Bolt EV">Chevrolet Bolt EV</a> in October 2016, the first ever mass market <a href="/wiki/All-electric_car" class="mw-redirect" title="All-electric car">all-electric car</a> with a range of more than 200 miles (320 km). Deliveries in California are scheduled to begin in late 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-SFG02042016_168-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SFG02042016-168">[167]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-EPAratings_169-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EPAratings-169">[168]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">[169]</a></sup> The vehicle will be launched in all 50 US states and analysts expect it to sell around 30,000 units per year, though GM itself has not confirmed these estimates. The battery pack and most drivetrain components are built by LG and assembled in GM's Lake Orion plant.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">[170]</a></sup></p><p>In March 2019, the company announced that it would begin production of a new EV model in Lake Orion but declined to provide details about the vehicle at that time.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">[171]</a></sup> In May 2019, General Motors received pushback on its plan to release a fleet of up to 2,500 modified Chevrolet Bolt electric vehicles. The company planned to release these vehicles by Q4 of 2019 as part of their initiatives to build a controlled self-driving fleet.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">[172]</a></sup></p><p>In January 2020, GM announced the return of the <a href="/wiki/Hummer" title="Hummer">Hummer</a> nameplate as a series of electric vehicles to be sold from within the <a href="/wiki/GMC_(automobile)" title="GMC (automobile)">GMC</a> portfolio, known as the <a href="/wiki/GMC_Hummer_EV" title="GMC Hummer EV">GMC Hummer EV</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">[173]</a></sup> The first vehicle, a pickup truck variant, will go on sale in late 2021 with over 1,000 horsepower, to be followed by an SUV sometime in 2022–2023.
</p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Battery_packs_for_electric_vehicles">Battery packs for electric vehicles</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=General_Motors&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Battery packs for electric vehicles" data-section="21" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>GM builds battery packs in southern <a href="/wiki/Michigan" title="Michigan">Michigan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-RSC_149-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RSC-149">[148]</a></sup> GM also established an automotive battery laboratory in Michigan.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">[174]</a></sup> GM will be responsible for battery management systems and power electronics, thermal management, as well as the pack assembly. An existing GM facility at Brownstown Township was chosen to be upgraded as battery pack plant.<sup id="cite_ref-RSC_149-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RSC-149">[148]</a></sup> LG Chem's U.S. subsidiary, Compact Power of Troy, Michigan, has been building the prototype packs for the development vehicles and will continue to provide integration support and act as a liaison for the program.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Hydrogen_initiative">Hydrogen initiative</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=General_Motors&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Hydrogen initiative" data-section="22" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:DSCN1474.JPG" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/DSCN1474.JPG/220px-DSCN1474.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 165px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/DSCN1474.JPG/220px-DSCN1474.JPG" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="165" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:DSCN1474.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/General_Motors_Sequel" class="mw-redirect" title="General Motors Sequel">Sequel</a>, a fuel cell-powered vehicle from GM</div></div></div>
<p>The 1966 GM Electrovan is credited with being the first hydrogen <a href="/wiki/Fuel_cell" title="Fuel cell">fuel cell</a> car ever produced.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">[175]</a></sup> Though fuel cells have been around since the early 1800s, General Motors was the first to use a fuel cell, supplied by Union Carbide, to power the wheels of a vehicle with a budget of "millions of dollars".<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">[176]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-AutonewsLongView_178-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AutonewsLongView-178">[177]</a></sup> In 2002, it was reported that GM spent about $100 million a year in research and development of fuel cell vehicle.<sup id="cite_ref-AutonewsLongView_178-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AutonewsLongView-178">[177]</a></sup> In June 2007, Larry Burns, vice president of research and development, said he was not yet willing to say exactly when hydrogen vehicles would be mass-produced, but he said it should happen before 2020, the year many experts have predicted. He said "I sure would be disappointed if we weren't there" before 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">[178]</a></sup></p><p>On July 2, 2013, GM and Honda announced a partnership to develop fuel cell systems and hydrogen storage technologies for the 2020 time frame. GM and Honda are leaders in fuel cell technology, ranking No. 1 and No. 2, respectively, in total fuel cell patents filed between 2002 and 2012, with more than 1,200 between them according to the Clean Energy Patent Growth Index.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Flexible-fuel_vehicles">Flexible-fuel vehicles</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=General_Motors&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Flexible-fuel vehicles" data-section="23" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Chevrolet_Impala_FlexFuel_34_MIA_12_2008_with_logo.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Chevrolet_Impala_FlexFuel_34_MIA_12_2008_with_logo.jpg/220px-Chevrolet_Impala_FlexFuel_34_MIA_12_2008_with_logo.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="1181" data-file-height="787"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 147px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Chevrolet_Impala_FlexFuel_34_MIA_12_2008_with_logo.jpg/220px-Chevrolet_Impala_FlexFuel_34_MIA_12_2008_with_logo.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="147" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Chevrolet_Impala_FlexFuel_34_MIA_12_2008_with_logo.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>E85 FlexFuel <a href="/wiki/Chevrolet_Impala" title="Chevrolet Impala">Chevrolet Impala</a> LT 2009 (USA)</div></div></div>
<p>GM produces several <a href="/wiki/Flexible-fuel_vehicle" title="Flexible-fuel vehicle">flexible-fuel vehicles</a> that can operate on <a href="/wiki/E85" title="E85">E85</a> <a href="/wiki/Ethanol_fuel" title="Ethanol fuel">ethanol fuel</a> or gasoline, or any blend of both. Since 2006 GM started featuring a bright yellow gas cap to remind drivers of the E85 capabilities.<sup id="cite_ref-USAToday_180-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USAToday-180">[179]</a></sup></p><p>GM is the leader in E85 flex fuel vehicles, with over 6 million FlexFuel vehicles on the road in the U.S. In 2010, GM pledged to have more than half of their annual vehicle production be E85 or <a href="/wiki/Biodiesel" title="Biodiesel">biodiesel</a> capable by 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">[180]</a></sup> As of 2012, GM offers 20 ethanol-enabled FlexFuel cars and trucks in the US, and offers more FlexFuel vehicles models than any other automaker.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">[181]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Hydrotec_Military_Vehicles">Hydrotec Military Vehicles</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=General_Motors&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Hydrotec Military Vehicles" data-section="24" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/GM_Defense" title="GM Defense">GM Defense</a> is the GM division leveraging GM's advanced technology propulsion systems, including Hydrotec Fuel Cell and Jouletec batteries for a variety of military applications including autonomous electric platforms and flex-fuel cell pickups converted for military use.
</p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(9)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Philanthropy">Philanthropy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=General_Motors&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Philanthropy" data-section="25" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-9 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-9">
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/General_Motors_Foundation" title="General Motors Foundation">General Motors Foundation</a></div>
<p>Since 1994, General Motors has donated over $23 million in cash and vehicles to the <a href="/wiki/Nature_Conservancy" class="mw-redirect" title="Nature Conservancy">Nature Conservancy</a>, and funding from GM supports many conservation projects.<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">[182]</a></sup></p><p>In 1996, GMC partnered with the fashion industry as a part of the <i>GM/CFDA Concept: Cure</i>, a collaboration between General Motors and the Fashion industry bringing awareness to and raising funds for breast cancer. The program involved five designers, each lending their artistic talents to customize five different vehicles. <a href="/wiki/Nicole_Miller" title="Nicole Miller">Nicole Miller</a>, <a href="/wiki/Richard_Tyler_(designer)" title="Richard Tyler (designer)">Richard Tyler</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anna_Sui" title="Anna Sui">Anna Sui</a>, <a href="/wiki/Todd_Oldham" title="Todd Oldham">Todd Oldham</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Mark_Eisen&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Mark Eisen (page does not exist)">Mark Eisen</a> were tasked with transforming a <a href="/wiki/Cadillac_STS" title="Cadillac STS">Cadillac STS</a>, <a href="/wiki/Buick_Riviera" title="Buick Riviera">Buick Riviera</a>, <a href="/wiki/GMC_Yukon" class="mw-redirect" title="GMC Yukon">GMC Yukon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oldsmobile_Bravada" title="Oldsmobile Bravada">Oldsmobile Bravada</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chevrolet_Camaro" title="Chevrolet Camaro">Chevrolet Camaro</a> Z28, respectively. The cars were then auctioned with the proceeds presented to the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Nina_Hyde&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Nina Hyde (page does not exist)">Nina Hyde</a> Center at the Greater Los Angeles Auto Show in 1997.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">[183]</a></sup></p><p>Since 1997, the GM Foundation has been a source of funding for <a href="/wiki/Safe_Kids_USA" class="mw-redirect" title="Safe Kids USA">Safe Kids USA</a>'s "Safe Kids Buckle Up" program, a national initiative to ensure child automobile safety through education and inspection.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">[184]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-WebWire-SKBU_186-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WebWire-SKBU-186">[185]</a></sup></p><p>Through 2002, the PACE Awards program, led by GM, EDS, and SUN Microsystems, has given over $1.2 billion of in-kind contributions which includes computers to over 18 universities to support engineering education.<sup id="cite_ref-pace_187-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pace-187">[186]</a></sup> In 2009, the GM led group has helped the Pace Awards program worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-PacePartners_188-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PacePartners-188">[187]</a></sup></p><p>In 2004, GM gave $51,200,000 in cash contributions and $17,200,000 in-kind donations to charitable causes.<sup id="cite_ref-donations_189-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-donations-189">[188]</a></sup></p><p>The General Motors Foundation (GM Foundation) receives philanthropic bequests from General Motors. It is a 501(c)(3) foundation incorporated in 1976.<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">[189]</a></sup></p><p>On March 21, 2020, following the <a href="/wiki/2019%E2%80%9320_coronavirus_pandemic" title="2019–20 coronavirus pandemic">coronavirus pandemic</a>, General Motors announced that they are working with <a href="/wiki/Ventec_Life_Systems" title="Ventec Life Systems">Ventec Life Systems</a> to produce ventilators. GM's CEO Mary Barra stated, "We are working closely with Ventec to rapidly scale up production of their critically important respiratory products to support our <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">country</a>'s fight again the COVID-19 pandemic." According to the statement, Ventec will borrow GM's resources and use their expertise to rapidly build new ventilators.<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">[190]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(10)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Branding">Branding</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=General_Motors&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Branding" data-section="26" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-10 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-10">
